## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The nonlinearity can arise from anharmonic restoring forces (Duffing-type), nonlinear damping, or external time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Asymmetric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (quadratic + cubic nonlinearity)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Damped driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal driving with damping)
- Nonlinear damping + Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (mixed nonlinearity)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (multiplicative coupling term)
- Softening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (generalized restoring force with damping)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (parametrically driven oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Symmetric restoring force potentials → only odd powers of x (x, x³, x⁵) in the acceleration expression
- Asymmetric potential wells → even powers of x (x²) appear alongside odd powers in restoring force
- Self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles) → velocity-dependent terms with sign changes, e.g., (1 - x²)*v structure
- Parametric excitation → time-dependent coefficients multiplying position, e.g., cos(ωt)*x
- Hardening vs softening springs → sign of cubic coefficient: positive x³ = hardening, negative x³ = softening
- Energy-dependent frequency → mixed terms like x²*v or v²*x indicate amplitude-dependent behavior
- Nonlinear drag → odd powers of velocity (v³, v⁵) preserve time-reversal antisymmetry of dissipation
- Phase-space rotation symmetry → terms that are functions of x² + c*v² indicate energy-based dynamics

**GT:** `-0.263437949946663*v*sin(x) - 0.526875899893326*v - 2.50712956886133*x + 0.460766280298364*sin(t)`

The key terms in the GT are:
1. `sin(t)` term (with coefficient)
2. `x` term (linear in x)
3. `v` term (linear in v)
4. `v*sin(x)` term

The critical challenge is the `v*sin(x)` term. None of the candidates explicitly contain `v*sin(x)`. Let me check if any candidate can produce this term through their structure.

Most candidates have terms like `v*x`, `x**2`, `x**3`, `v*x**2`, etc. - these are polynomial terms that cannot reproduce `v*sin(x)`.

The `sin(t)` term in the GT can be matched by `exp(c3*t)*sin(c4*t + c5)` by setting `c3=0`, `c4=1`, `c5=0` (giving `c2*sin(t)`).

Let me look for candidates with `v*x*exp(c*x)` or similar terms that might approximate `v*sin(x)` — but no, we need **exact** equivalence for all x, not approximation.

The term `v*sin(x)` is a transcendental function of x multiplied by v. To match this exactly, a candidate would need to produce `sin(x)` somehow. Let me check:

- `log(c*x + 1)` — this is logarithmic, not sinusoidal
- `exp(c*x)` — exponential, not sinusoidal
- `x**n` — polynomial terms
- `v*x*exp(c*x)` — this is `v*x*exp(c*x)`, which for no value of c equals `v*sin(x)`
- `x**2*exp(c*x)` — similar issue
- `exp(c*x**2)` — Gaussian-like, not sin

None of these functional forms can produce `sin(x)` for any parameter values. The function `sin(x)` cannot be represented as any finite combination of polynomials in x, exponentials `exp(c*x)`, `exp(c*x^2)`, logarithms `log(c*x+1)`, or products thereof.

The `sin` function only appears in the candidates as `sin(c*t + c)` (a function of t), never as a function of x. Therefore, no candidate can produce the `v*sin(x)` term.

Let me double-check: is there any candidate where the `v*sin(x)` term could be absorbed or cancelled? No — the GT requires `v*sin(x)` to be present, and since `sin(x)` is linearly independent from all polynomial and exponential functions of x, no combination of the terms available in any candidate can produce it.

Going through all 50 candidates systematically: every single one lacks the ability to generate a `v*sin(x)` term. The candidates contain terms that are polynomials in x (like `x`, `x**2`, `x**3`, `x**5`), exponentials in x (`exp(c*x)`, `exp(c*x**2)`), logarithms (`log(c*x+1)`), products of v with polynomials/exponentials in x (`v*x`, `v*x**2`, `v*x*exp(c*x)`), and sinusoidal functions only in t (`sin(c*t+c)`). None can produce `sin(x)`.

The GT contains these basis functions:
1. `v*sin(x)` - product of v with sin(x)
2. `v` - linear in v
3. `x` - linear in x
4. `sin(t)` - sine of t

Key observation: The GT has `sin(t)` and `v*sin(x)`. The candidates all have `exp(c*t)*sin(c*t + c)` for the time-dependent term. For this to match `sin(t)`, we need `c3=0` (so exp term becomes 1), `c4=1`, and appropriate `c5`.

Also critically, the GT has `v*sin(x)` which is a nonlinear coupling. None of the polynomial/exponential terms in the candidates can produce `sin(x)`. Let me check each candidate for the presence of `v*sin(x)`.

Looking through ALL candidates: Every single candidate uses polynomial terms in x (like `x`, `x**2`, `x**3`, `x**5`), exponential terms in x (like `exp(c*x)`), logarithmic terms (like `log(c*x+1)`), or products of these with v. **None of them contain `sin(x)` or any trigonometric function of x.**

The GT requires `v*sin(x)` which is `-0.263437949946663*v*sin(x)`. This term cannot be represented by:
- Polynomial terms in x (by linear independence of sin(x) and polynomials)
- `v*x*exp(c*x)` terms (exponentials are linearly independent from sin)
- `log(c*x+1)` terms
- Any combination of the above

Since `sin(x)` is linearly independent from all polynomials, exponentials, and logarithms, no finite combination of these basis functions can exactly equal `sin(x)` for all x. The coefficient of `v*sin(x)` in the GT is `-0.2634...` which is non-zero, so this term cannot be ignored.

Therefore, **none of the candidates can match the GT**, because none contain `sin(x)` as a basis function, and `v*sin(x)` cannot be expressed using the basis functions available in any candidate.

Let me verify this conclusion by checking each candidate systematically:

Candidates 1-50: All use combinations of `x`, `x**2`, `x**3`, `x**5`, `v*x`, `v*x**2`, `v**2`, `v**3`, `v**2*x`, `exp(c*x)`, `x**2*exp(c*x)`, `v*x*exp(c*x)`, `log(c*x+1)`, `exp(c*x**2)`, `exp(c*v)`, `t*x**3`, `x*cos(c*t)`, `v*exp(c*t)`, `log(c*t+1)`, `t*(c+x)**3` — but **none contain `sin(x)`**.
